Lensing features of confirmed systems and properties of associated redMAPPer clusters. In the left section, we show the DESDM object IDs for lenses (as in Table 1), the source image IDs, and the emission lines identified in the source spectra. In the middle section, we show the photometric redshifts of lenses zlens, spectroscopic redshifts zspec, Einstein radii thetaE, and derived enclosed masses Menc. Ellipsis points indicate features that were not measured. For all of the systems, photometric redshifts (drawn from the the DESDM database) were obtained for the lensing galaxies. The uncertainties have been multiplied by 1.5 times the original estimate, according to the results of Sanchez et al. (2014) for estimating uncertainties in DES photometric redshift measurement codes. The photometric redshifts of the sources within the DESDM database were not found to be reliable when compared with the spectroscopic redshift measurements made in this work: the source redshifts are too large for accurate photometric estimations. Redshifts for the sources are those measured from spectroscopic follow-up at Gemini South and Magellan; please see Section 4 for details of the spectroscopic follow-up. Only one lensing galaxy has a spectroscopic redshift: in DES J0330-5228, we used that measured by Werner et al. (2007). For five of the six systems, morphology indicates a single Einstein radius and enclosed mass for a given system. For each of the systems DES J0221-0646 and DES J0446-5126, we measured a single Einstein radius that intersects two images with the same source redshift. DES J0250-0008 and DES J0330-5228 each have only one source image with redshifts. DES J0329-2820 has two source redshifts, but only one is chosen for the radius measurement. In DES J2336-5352, the lower-redshift source has, anomalously, a larger radius; arc B may be outside the caustic and thus only weakly magnified and not multiply imaged. Please see Sections 5.1-5.6 for details of the analysis in each system. In the rightmost section, we show the properties of the associated redMAPPer clusters. The masses are measured with the methods of Saro et al. (2015). The mass calibration method does not reach to low enough masses and richness to provide a complete probability distribution for the mass of this DES J0221-0646; we instead cite an upper limit. The redMAPPer redshifts are measured for the entire cluster with the colors of all the cluster members, which affords a much smaller uncertainty in the redMAPPer redshifts than that of the lensing galaxy for all systems.", "Table captions or footers": {"Info after table 6": "\n", "Info after table 4": "\n", "Info after table 7": "Note. <main role=\"main\">\n        <!-- Secondary header starts -->\n<div class=\"secondary-header cf\" id=\"wd-secondary-header\">\n    <!-- Branded journal header starts -->\n<div class=\"big-branded\">\n\n    <div class=\"publication-name\" id=\"wd-pub-name\">\n\t<div class=\"publication-title\" itemprop=\"name\" itemid=\"periodical\">\n\t\t\t\t<!-- Journal image link tile starts -->\n<!-- Logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"/journal/0004-637X\" itemprop=\"url\">\n    <img src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/8febf88b-d09c-11e5-b0b6-759f86a2008e/apj-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Astrophysical Journal\">\n</a>\n<!-- Logo tile ends -->\n<!-- Journal image link tile ends -->\n</div>\n\t\t</div>\n    <div class=\"partner-logos m-hide\" id=\"wd-partner-logos\">\n            <div class=\"partner-logo-alignment\">\n                <!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/8a2230b8-d09c-11e5-b0b6-759f86a2008e/aas-2018.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The American Astronomical Society, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/8a2230b8-d09c-11e5-b0b6-759f86a2008e/aas-2018.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The American Astronomical Society, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<p></p>\n                </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n<!-- Branded journal header ends -->\n</div> <!-- end secondary-header -->\n<!-- Secondary header ends --><div class=\"da1-da2\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle\" id=\"page-content\">\n            <div class=\"da1 ta1 article-head\">\n                <!-- Start Eyebrow block, containing Surtitle and Labels -->\n<div class=\"eyebrow\">\n\t<!-- Start Collection Labels -->\n    <!-- End Collection Labels --> </div>\n<!-- End Eyebrow block -->\n\n<h1 itemprop=\"headline\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-title\">OBSERVATION AND CONFIRMATION OF SIX STRONG-LENSING SYSTEMS IN THE DARK ENERGY SURVEY SCIENCE VERIFICATION DATA<SUP>*</SUP>  </h1>\n\n<p class=\"mb-0\">\n\t<span data-authors=\"\">\n\t\t<span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">B. <span class=\"icon-newtab\">\n            </a></p>\n        </div>\n\n    <!-- End Email Alert -->\n<!-- End Email Alert --><!-- Start Citation Alert Link -->\n                        <p>\n<div class=\"jnl-notifications-wrapper\">\n    <a class=\"wd-jnl-email-alert\" href=\"https://myiopscience.iop.org/signin?origin=a0&return=https%3A%2F%2Fiopscience.iop.org%2Fmyiopscience%2Falerts%2Fsubscribe%3FarticleID%3D0004-637X%2F827%2F1%2F51\"><span\n            class=\"icon-alarm icon-alarm--jhp\"></span>Create citation alert</a>\n</div><!-- End Citation Alert Link -->\n                    </div>\n\t\t</div>\n    </div>\n    <!-- Article information ends -->\n<!-- Start Info top-->\n    <!-- end Info top --><div class=\"article-content\">\n\t<span id=\"articleId\" class=\"hide\">0004-637X/827/1/51</span>\n<!-- Start Abstract -->\n    <h2 id=\"artAbst\" class=\"collapse-blocked\">Abstract</h2>\n        <!-- Start article video abstract -->\n\t<!-- End article video abstract -->\n\t<div class=\"article-text wd-jnl-art-abstract cf\" itemprop=\"description\">\n             <P>We report the observation and confirmation of the first group- and cluster-scale strong gravitational lensing systems found in Dark Energy Survey data. Through visual inspection of data from the Science Verification season, we identified 53 candidate systems. We then obtained spectroscopic follow-up of 21 candidates using the Gemini Multi-object Spectrograph at the Gemini South telescope and the Inamori-Magellan Areal Camera and Spectrograph at the Magellan/Baade telescope. With this follow-up, we confirmed six candidates as gravitational lenses: three of the systems are newly discovered, and the remaining three were previously known. Of the 21 observed candidates, the remaining 15 either were not detected in spectroscopic observations, were observed and did not exhibit continuum emission (or spectral features), or were ruled out as lensing systems. The confirmed sample consists of one group-scale and five galaxy-cluster-scale lenses. The lensed sources range in redshift <I>z</I> ~ 0.80\u20133.2 and in <I>i</I>-band surface brightness <I>i</I> <SUB>SB</SUB> ~ 23\u201325 mag arcsec<SUP>\u22122</SUP> (2'' aperture). For each of the six systems, we estimate the Einstein radius <I>\u03b8</I> <SUB>E</SUB> and the enclosed mass <I>M</I> <SUB>enc</SUB>, which have ranges <I>\u03b8</I> <SUB>E</SUB> ~ 5''\u20139'' and <I>M</I> <SUB>enc</SUB> ~ 8 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 10<SUP>12</SUP> to 6 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 10<SUP>13</SUP> <I>M</I> <SUB>\u2299</SUB>, respectively.</P> </div>\n    <!-- End abstract -->\n<!-- Start Export citation and abstract tools -->\n\t<p>\n\t\t<small>Export citation and abstract</small>\n\t\t<span class=\"btn-multi-block\">\n\t\t\t<a href=\"http://nedwww.ipac.caltech.edu/cgi-bin/nph-objsearch?refcode=2016ApJ...827...51N&search_type=Search \" target=\"_blank\">NED Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a bottom -->\n<!-- Start article full text -->\n\t<div xmlns:book=\"http://api.iop.org/Book/1.0/\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-full-text article-text\">\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaa23f2s1\" name=\"apjaa23f2s1\">1.\u00a0INTRODUCTION</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Strong gravitational lensing of galaxies and quasars provides opportunities to study cosmology, dark matter, dark energy, galactic structure, and galaxy evolution (Treu <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib75\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib75\">2010</a>). Strong lensing also provides a sample of galaxies\u2014the lenses themselves\u2014that are selected based on total mass, rather than luminosity or surface brightness (e.g., Reblinsky &amp; Bartelmann <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib64\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib64\">1999</a>): the distortion of images by the lens depends only on the total lens mass and its spatial distribution.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2fn2\">52</a></sup>\n\n</p><p>The majority of strong-lensing systems discovered in the past decade were found with a variety of techniques, mostly through dedicated investigations of existing data or through new dedicated surveys. Data from the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (York et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib83\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib83\">2000</a>), for example, have been used by a number of groups to select lens candidates. The Optimal Line-of-Sight-lens Survey (Willis et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib82\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib82\">2006</a>) discovered five galaxy-scale lenses. Investigating a sample of rich galaxy clusters, Hennawi et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib35\">2008</a>) found 37 lenses of varying size and morphology. The Sloan Bright Arc Survey (SBAS; Allam et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib2\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib2\">2007</a>; Kubik <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib42\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib42\">2007</a>; Diehl et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib25\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib25\">2009</a>; Kubo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib43\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib43\">2009</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib44\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib44\">2010</a>; Lin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib47\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib47\">2009</a>; Wiesner et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib81\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib81\">2012</a>) discovered 28 galaxy- and group-scale systems. The Sloan Lens ACS Survey group (Bolton et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib13\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib13\">2008</a>) identified 137 lensing candidates, using both the spectroscopic and imaging catalogs. The CAmbridge Sloan Survey Of Wide ARcs in the skY (Belokurov et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib4\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib4\">2009</a>) searched for wide-separation, galaxy-scale systems, uncovering 45 systems to date. Other searches, like the Strong Lensing Legacy Survey (SL2S; e.g., Cabanac et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib17\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib17\">2007</a>; More et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib57\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib57\">2012</a>), have yielded 127 lens candidates\u2014spanning group to cluster scales\u2014from ~150 deg<sup>2</sup> of sky area in the Canada\u2013France\u2013Hawaii Telescope Legacy Survey (CFHTLS). Searches in the COSMOS field (Faure et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib29\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib29\">2008</a>; Jackson <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib38\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib38\">2008</a>) have yielded 70 lens candidates.</p><p>Surveys in other bands have also proven successful. The Cosmic Lens All-Sky Survey<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2fn3\">53</a></sup>\n (CLASS; e.g., Browne et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib14\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib14\">2003</a>; Myers et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib58\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib58\">2003</a>; York et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib84\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib84\">2005</a>) confirmed nearly 25 radio-loud galaxy-scale lensing systems. Several of them have multiply imaged sources, including the four-image system CLASS B2045+265 (Fassnacht et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib28\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib28\">1999</a>) and the two-component wide-separation (4<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />56) system CLASS B2108+213 (McKean et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib51\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib51\">2005</a>).</p><p>There is a history of targeting massive galaxy clusters to use as cosmic lenses for the study of high-redshift star-forming galaxies in the infrared (e.g., Smail et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib72\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib72\">1997</a>; Egami et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib27\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib27\">2010</a>; Swinbank et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib74\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib74\">2010</a>). Recently, wide-field millimeter and submillimeter surveys have enabled the discovery of new populations of strong-lensing systems based on a simple flux-density selection (Blain <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib10\">1996</a>; Negrello et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib60\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib60\">2007</a>) with near-100% completeness (Negrello et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib61\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib61\">2010</a>; Vieira et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib78\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib78\">2010</a>; Bussmann et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib16\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib16\">2013</a>). These wide-field surveys, coupled with the recently commissioned Atacama Large Millimeter Array (ALMA), have opened a new window to star formation at high redshifts (e.g., Vieira et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib79\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib79\">2013</a>; ALMA Partnership et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib3\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib3\">2015</a>).</p><p>These investigations\u2014from optical to millimeter wavebands\u2014produced on the order of 1000 lensing candidates or confirmed lenses, spanning a range of arc sizes\u2014from small arcs (<em>\u03b8</em><sub>E</sub> ~ 3'') produced by single-galaxy lenses to giant arcs typically found in clusters (<em>\u03b8</em><sub>E</sub> ~ 10'').</p><p>The Dark Energy Survey (DES<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2fn4\">54</a></sup>\n; Diehl et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib24\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib24\">2014</a>; Flaugher et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib30\">2015</a>)\u2014a new, deep sky survey covering 5000 deg<sup>2</sup> of the Southern Galactic Cap in five optical filters (<em>grizY</em>)\u2014is suitable for a systematic census of gravitational lenses. The wide-field survey will have a depth of <em>i</em> ~ 24 mag at 10<em>\u03c3</em> detection threshold, and the 30 deg<sup>2</sup>  supernova survey is spread over 10 fields\u2014eight shallow and two deep. The primary instrument for DES is the newly assembled Dark Energy Camera (DECam), a wide-field (3 deg<sup>2</sup>) CCD mosaic camera located on the Blanco 4 m telescope at the Cerro Tololo Inter-American Observatory in the Chilean Andes. The DES footprint is best observed between August and mid-February. DES observes for ~105 nights yr<sup>\u22121</sup> and has completed 3 of the 5 yr of planned observations. The survey will produce the widest, deepest, and most uniform contiguous map in optical wavelengths of the southern sky, much of which has not been systematically surveyed\u2014and not at such depth\u2014until now. These features make DES suitable for finding many strong-lensing systems that span large ranges in redshift and Einstein radii. DES expects to uncover a large and diverse sample of strong gravitational lenses, which will provide for a rich science program.</p><p>One of the main objectives of the strong-lensing science program in DES is to derive constraints on dark energy. One of the two key components will be exploiting galaxy- and cluster-scale lenses that have multiple background sources at different redshifts. When there exist two lensed sources, one source will lie between the lens and the other, more distant source: these sources produce distinct Einstein radii. The ratio of the Einstein radii (and thus, a ratio of angular diameter distances) is independent of the Hubble constant and only weakly dependent on the lens mass distribution. Provided that the lensing mass can be well modeled, the ratio of distance ratios can help to constrain dark energy models (Gavazzi et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib34\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib34\">2008</a>; Jullo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib40\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib40\">2010</a>; Collett et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib21\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib21\">2012</a>; Collett &amp; Auger <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib20\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib20\">2014</a>).</p><p>The second key component is to use strongly lensed quasars to measure cosmological parameters (e.g., <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>) by utilizing the time delays between multiple images (Refsdal <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib65\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib65\">1964</a>; Suyu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib73\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib73\">2013</a>; Birrer et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib9\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib9\">2015</a>) of time-varying sources. We predict that the wide-field survey should contain about 120 lensed quasars brighter than <em>i</em> = 21 mag (Oguri &amp; Marshall <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib62\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib62\">2010</a>), of which ~20 would be high-information-content quadruple-image configurations. Through the STRong-lensing Insights into DES (STRIDES) program,<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2fn5\">55</a></sup>\n DES has discovered and confirmed two lensed quasars so far at <em>z</em> ~ 1.6 and ~2.4 (Agnello et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib1\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib1\">2015</a>). In addition, 30 deg<sup>2</sup> of deep imaging in the supernova fields, which have a high cadence, provides an opportunity to find lensed supernovae.</p><p>In addition to constraining cosmology, we will use a substantial cluster-scale lens sample to study dark matter mass profiles. Also, we expect to discover a large sample of sources at varying redshifts that will be valuable for studies of galaxy evolution.</p><p>In this paper, we report on the search for strong lens systems from the DES Science Verification (SV) data. We performed a visual inspection of the ~250 deg<sup>2</sup>  SV area, discovering a large number of candidates, which we then culled to 53 high-ranking candidates. We selected 24 for spectroscopic follow-up and were able to observe 21 of them. Of the sample we followed up, we focus on six systems that have compelling evidence (color, morphology, and spectroscopy) of strong gravitational lensing: three of these are newly identified, and three are already known from other surveys. We have spectroscopically confirmed these six systems (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa23f2f1\">1</a>) as strong gravitational lensing systems.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaa23f2f1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa23f2f1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/827/1/51/Full/apjaa23f2f1_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 1.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/827/1/51/Full/apjaa23f2f1_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 1.</strong>\u00a0Color coadded DES images of the six systems described in this work: (a) DES J0221\u20130646, (b) DES J0250\u20130008, (c) DES J0329\u20132820, (d) DES J0330\u20135228, (e) DES J0446\u20135126, (f) DES J2336\u20135352. All images are oriented north up, east left, and are 1' <b>&#x00d7;</b> 1' in area. The lensing features targeted for spectroscopy are indicated by the letters. Refer to Figures <a href=\"#apjaa23f2f2\">2</a>\u2013<a href=\"#apjaa23f2f7\">7</a> for a more detailed view of the field and the image candidates.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaa23f2f1\" href=\"/0004-637X/827/1/51/downloadFigure/figure/apjaa23f2f1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaa23f2f1\" href=\"/0004-637X/827/1/51/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaa23f2f1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>Several of the candidate systems were selected for the possibility of housing sources at multiple redshifts, key for our dark energy studies. While we do not endeavor in this work to perform detailed mass modeling of cluster-scale lenses with DES data, future higher-resolution imaging follow-up may allow for detailed modeling of cluster mass distributions.</p><p>The paper is organized as follows. In Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2s2\">2</a> we describe the DES SV season data. In Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2s3\">3</a> we present the lens search, followed by the spectroscopic follow-up in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2s4\">4</a>. We present the six confirmed systems and their properties in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2s5\">5</a>, discuss results in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2s6\">6</a>, and conclude in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2s7\">7</a>. All magnitudes are in the AB system. We assume a flat, Planck \u039bCDM cosmology: \u03a9<sub>M</sub> = 0.308, \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub> = 0.692, and <em>H</em><sub>0</sub> = 67.8 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup> (Planck Collaboration et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib63\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib63\">2015</a>).</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaa23f2s2\" name=\"apjaa23f2s2\">2.\u00a0DES SV DATA</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>The SV observing season took place from 2012 November 1 to 2013 February 23, immediately after the commissioning of the DECam (Flaugher et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib30\">2015</a>). The survey started in 2013 August and has completed three seasons beyond SV. The survey and operations for SV and Year 1 are described in Diehl et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib24\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib24\">2014</a>).</p><p>In total, SV observations cover ~250 deg<sup>2</sup> in five optical filter bands (<em>grizY</em>), nearly reaching the expected full 5 yr depth of DES: below, we report median depth estimates of these data at 10<em>\u03c3</em> galaxy limiting magnitude. The wide-field survey consists of the SPT-E and SPT-W fields that are located, respectively, in the east and west regions of the South Pole Telescope (SPT) survey footprint (Carlstrom et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib18\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib18\">2011</a>): the <em>g</em>-band depth extends to ~24.5 mag. The 30 deg<sup>2</sup> supernova survey takes place in eight shallow fields and two deep fields, extending to <em>g</em>-band depths, 25.0 and 25.4 mag, respectively.</p><p>The DES data management (DESDM) team was responsible for the reduction of the SV images. The basic reductions and coadd source detection were performed by DESDM (Desai et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib23\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib23\">2012</a>; R. Gruendl 2015, in preparation): the software for reduction of SV exposures is similar to that used in the Y1A1 release.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2fn6\">56</a></sup>\n The detrended, single-epoch images were calibrated, background-subtracted, and combined into \"coadd tiles.\" Each coadd tile has dimensions 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />72 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />72, so defined as to cover the entire DES footprint. A catalog of objects was extracted from the coadded images using Source Extractor (SExtractor; Bertin &amp; Arnouts <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib7\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib7\">1996</a>; Bertin <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib6\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib6\">2011</a>). Unless otherwise stated, photometric and position data of all objects in this work originate in this object catalog (see Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2t1\">1</a>).</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaa23f2t1\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 1.</b>\u00a0\nProperties of Lensing Systems: Positions and Photometry of Lenses and Source Images\n</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa23f2t1\" data-toolbar-img=\"/0004-637X/827/1/51/suppdata/apjaa23f2t1_lr.gif\" data-toolbar-type=\"table\" data-toolbar-title=\"Table 1\"><colgroup><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col></colgroup><thead>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">System ID and</th>\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Object ID</th>\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">R.A. strong-lensing system. Source Image ID refers to the arc or lensed source image discussed in the text, in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa23f2f1\">1</a> and Figures <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa23f2f2\">2</a>\u2013<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa23f2f7\">7</a>. The Object ID is the unique identification number in the DESDM database of coadd objects. All positions (R.A., decl. in J2000) and magnitudes are drawn from the DESDM database, except in the case of source image B2 of DES J0446\u20135126: for this object, we measured aperture magnitudes via the Graphical Astronomy and Image Analysis software tool (GAIA <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib32\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib32\">2015</a>). <em>Y</em>-band photometry is provided where available: supernova fields were only observed in <em>Y</em>band for those fields that overlap with the wide-field survey, and arc B of DES J0329\u20132820 was too faint for detection in both DESDM and GAIA. Alternative identifications related to prior observations of some systems are listed as footnotes to this table.</p>\n<a name=\"apjaa23f2fn7\" id=\"apjaa23f2fn7\"></a><sup> a</sup>Object SA39: from More et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib57\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib57\">2012</a>).\n<a name=\"apjaa23f2fn8\" id=\"apjaa23f2fn8\"></a><sup> b</sup>SPT-CL J0330\u20135228/ACT-CL J0330\u20135227: from Bleem et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib11\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib11\">2015</a>).\n<a name=\"apjaa23f2fn9\" id=\"apjaa23f2fn9\"></a><sup> c</sup>Associated with radio source SUMSS J033057\u2013522811 (Mauch et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib50\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib50\">2003</a>; Werner et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib80\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib80\">2007</a>).\n<a name=\"apjaa23f2fn10\" id=\"apjaa23f2fn10\"></a><sup> d</sup>SCSO J233607\u2013535235: from Menanteau et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib53\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib53\">2010a</a>).\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/827/1/51/suppdata/apjaa23f2t1_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/0004-637X/827/1/51\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/827/1/51/suppdata/apjaa23f2t1_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaa23f2s3\" name=\"apjaa23f2s3\">3.\u00a0LENS SEARCH</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>The lens search, carried out by visually inspecting images, relied on morphology and color to identify lens candidates. We searched for arc- and ring-like features and multiply imaged sources, in association with red lensing galaxies or galaxy groups. Among the more typical of search criteria is the existence of blue source images in association with red galaxies, but some systems with red source images were also identified.</p><p>Although modern algorithms for automated arc- and ring-finders have improved in recent years, they still typically require manual intervention and/or subsequent visual inspection and verification (Lenzen et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib46\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib46\">2004</a>; Horesh et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib37\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib37\">2005</a>; Seidel &amp; Bartelmann <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib71\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib71\">2007</a>; Marshall et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib49\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib49\">2009</a>; More et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib57\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib57\">2012</a>; Joseph et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib39\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib39\">2014</a>). We performed a visual search without automated finders, because the SV sky area is relatively small and visual inspection is likely to recover the highest-ranking candidates that would be found with an automated finder. Given these search criteria, as well as the pixel scale of DECam and the seeing of DES data, there is a bias toward larger Einstein radii, and thus higher mass (depending on the source redshift(s)), which are easier to identify through visual inspection.</p><p>We performed two types of visual scans. We performed a nontargeted search of all ~250 deg<sup>2</sup>\u2014not focusing on any specific target regions or objects\u2014as well as a targeted scan of previously identified galaxy clusters. The visual scan is performed on false-color PNG images, which are made by combining <em>g</em>, <em>r</em>, <em>i</em> coadd tiles (defined in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2s2\">2</a>) into color images.</p><p>The nontargeted search was carried out by about 20 inspectors, who systematically examined all the tiles. The open-area search yielded a sample of ~1000 objects. Among the results of this search is the Cosmic Horseshoe (Belokurov et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib5\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib5\">2007</a>), which was then removed from our sample of follow-up candidates.</p><p>We also carried out two targeted searches. The first one was carried out around the 67 known clusters from the SPT SZ survey (Bleem et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib11\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib11\">2015</a>). Many of these clusters already have optical imaging follow-up and known lensing features. We identified nine candidates from this search. The second targeted search examined 374 galaxy clusters of richness &gt;50, which themselves were found using the red-sequence Matched-filter Probabilistic Percolation cluster-finder algorithm (redMAPPer; Rykoff et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib68\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib68\">2014</a>). This search yielded 39 candidates. The targeted search recovered known, confirmed lensing systems, such as BCS J2352\u20135452 (Buckley-Geer et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib15\">2011</a>), RXC J2248.7\u20134431 (B\u00f6hringer et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib12\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib12\">2004</a>), and ACT-CL J0102\u20134915 (El Gordo; Menanteau et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib55\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib55\">2012</a>), which we then removed from the sample of candidates for spectroscopic follow-up.</p><p>The combined nontargeted and targeted search samples were merged and assessed by a team of experienced inspectors. Most of these objects were not convincing as strong lens system candidates or were not bright enough to expect successful spectroscopic follow-up. Each of the systems was assigned a rank, 1 to 3\u2014with 1 signifying least likely to be a lens system, and 3 the most likely\u2014on the basis of morphology, color, and brightness of sources. This ranking resulted in 53 promising (\"rank 3\") candidates.</p><p>To characterize the selection function of our sample, we compare to a sample of 87 high-quality candidates and confirmed lensing systems found in CFHTLS data. It includes a sample of 33 confirmed lenses from the <span class=\"small-caps\">RingFinder</span> (Gavazzi et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib33\">2014</a>), the 26 most promising candidates from <span class=\"small-caps\">ArcFinder</span> as implemented in SL2S ARCS (SARCS; More et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib57\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib57\">2012</a>), and 28 candidates from <span class=\"small-caps\">SpaceWarps</span> (More et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib56\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib56\">2016</a>), giving a total of 87 objects; the Einstein radii have a range of 1'' &lt; <em>\u03b8</em><sub>E</sub> &lt; 18''. In the <span class=\"small-caps\">ArcFinder</span> search, 12 candidates have giant arcs, which canonically have length-to-width ratio \u22658. CFHTLS has an effective search area of ~150 deg<sup>2</sup> and depths of <em>g</em> ~ 25.5 and ~26.5 mag in wide and deep fields, respectively.</p><p>We estimate the lens-finding selection function of DES by counting the sources from the high-quality CFHTLS sample that survive a cut on the DES magnitude limit, which is taken to be 24.5 mag in <em>g</em>band for both the SV and full wide-field data. The source magnitudes of the samples listed above were provided by the author (A. More 2016, personal communication, 2015 November 11), and the calculation of the source magnitudes is discussed in Section 5.3 of More et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib56\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib56\">2016</a>). After performing the magnitude cut, we linearly scaled the resulting counts by the ratio of the survey areas. From this comparison, we estimate that the full DES Wide-field survey will contain 2100 promising candidates. Scaling the area again for the DES SV area, we expect 105 promising candidates, which is nearly twice the amount found in the search discussed in this work.</p><p>A few factors likely contributed to the difference between the number of lens system candidates expected and discovered in DES SV data. The nontargeted search was performed by scanning large images, rather than cutouts around particular objects, as was done with the targeted search around clusters. In addition, some regions were only scanned once during the nontargeted search. Rigorous characterization of a strong lens candidate selection function requires the construction of a framework to measure each scanner's efficiency, completeness, and purity. Such a program was not implemented for the SV searches.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaa23f2s4\" name=\"apjaa23f2s4\">4.\u00a0SPECTROSCOPIC FOLLOW-UP</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We obtained spectroscopic follow-up observations with the Gemini Multi-object Spectrograph (GMOS; Hook et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib36\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib36\">2004</a>) on the Gemini South Telescope, as part of the Gemini Large and Long Program GS-2014B-LP-5,<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2fn11\">57</a></sup>\n and with the Inamori-Magellan Areal Camera and Spectrograph (IMACS) multi-object spectrograph (Dressler et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib26\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib26\">2011</a>) on the Magellan/Baade Telescope.</p><p>Of the 53 high-ranking candidates found during the lens search, we selected the 24 candidates most suitable for spectroscopic follow-up. For the purposes of planning the follow-up, the 24 candidates were ranked (1\u20133) by their surface brightness, which is calculated using a 2''-diameter aperture in the <em>i</em>band:</p><ul class=\"clear-list wd-inline-list\"><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">1.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">R1: <em>i</em><sub>SB</sub> &lt; 23 mag arcsec<sup>\u22122</sup> (6 candidates);</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">2.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">R2: 23 &lt; <em>i</em><sub>SB</sub> &lt; 24 mag arcsec<sup>\u22122</sup> (14 candidates);</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">3.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">R3: <em>i</em><sub>SB</sub> &gt; 24 mag arcsec<sup>\u22122</sup> (4 candidates).</div></li></ul><p>These rankings are not related to the quality rankings of candidates in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2s3\">3</a>. Details of the observing parameters and conditions for each of our confirmed lensing systems are shown in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2t2\">2</a>. We acquired spectroscopic follow-up for 21 of the 24 candidate systems: 17 systems were observed at Gemini and 5 at Magellan. One of the systems, DES J0329\u20132820, was observed at both Gemini and Magellan: only B600 data were acquired at Gemini, which presented no spectral features, so we observed at longer wavelengths at Magellan.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaa23f2t2\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 2.</b>\u00a0\nSpectroscopic Observation Log\n</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa23f2t2\" data-toolbar-img=\"/0004-637X/827/1/51/suppdata/apjaa23f2t2_lr.gif\" data-toolbar-type=\"table\" data-toolbar-title=\"Table 22</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Gemini-GMOS</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">R150</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">1</td>\n<td align=\"center\">2014 Oct 19, 23</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Gemini-GMOS</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">B600/R150</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">1/1.63</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">0.64/0.67</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">DES J2336\u20135352</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">2014 Oct 21</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Gemini-GMOS</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">R150</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">1</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">0.73</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table><p><small>\n<p><strong>Note.</strong> Observation log for follow-up spectroscopic observations. DES ID is derived from the R.A. and decl. position of the lensing object at the center of the system. For the Gemini observations, seeing is taken from the Gemini Observation Logs, which keep environmental conditions in 2 hr increments: the seeing for each exposure set is interpolated for the time of observation between adjacent recordings of the environmental log. For the Magellan observation, seeing is measured from the FWHM of the PSFs of the acquisition stars in the science exposures.</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/827/1/51/suppdata/apjaa23f2t2_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/0004-637X/827/1/51\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/827/1/51/suppdata/apjaa23f2t2_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>We searched the Master Lens Database (L. Moustakas &amp; J. Brownstein 2016, in preparation)<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2fn12\">58</a></sup>\n and the Gemini Science Archive<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2fn13\">59</a></sup>\n to ascertain whether any of our candidates had been previously discovered or confirmed. The Master Lens Database (last updated 2015 November 17) contains 657 candidates and confirmed systems. Out of these systems, 44 fall within our search area but were not identified as candidates for our follow-up program. They were identified by various programs, such as SL2S, SPT, and searches in GEMS and <em>HST</em> fields. About half of these candidates have estimated Einstein radii <em>\u03b8</em><sub>E</sub> &lt; 2'', and the maximum radius is ~6''; at least 80% are galaxy-scale lenses. Of the 44 candidates, the lensing features are barely visible or better in DES SV data for about one-third of the systems, but they are only obvious for a few. The limited resolution of the DES images obscures lensing features, especially for smaller-radius systems. Additionally, many features are faint and are not obviously lensing features, but could be chance projection or on-edge spirals, for example.</p><p>The only candidate that is in our confirmed sample is SA39 (More et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib57\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib57\">2012</a>), discovered by the SL2S in CFHTLS data. We have obtained the first spectroscopic confirmation that SA39 is a strong-lensing system. This is DES J0221\u20130646 in our sample, and we present its confirmation in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2s5-1\">5.1</a>.</p><p>From the estimates of the selection function, we expect to find 105 promising candidates in DES, but we recovered 54. If all of the 44 missed candidates from the Master Lens Database are considered promising, then that would account for the discrepancy with our expectations described in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2s3\">3</a>. It is clear, however, that the image resolution is the principal factor in identification of systems with small Einstein radii.</p><h3 id=\"apjaa23f2s4-1\" name=\"apjaa23f2s4-1\">4.1.\u00a0Gemini/GMOS</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We observed some of the lensing candidates at Gemini South using the multi-object mode on GMOS. The mask for each field was centered on the candidate lens of each system, and slits were placed on the candidate source images. In some cases, it was necessary to shift the field center to locate a suitable guide star. Accommodating as many source targets as possible sometimes required rotation of the slit mask (i.e., rotation of the position angle of each system). We placed slits on as many of the lensing features as possible, and the remaining ~50 slits were placed on galaxy targets for photometric-redshift calibration of DES data. The slits were 1'' in width and of varying length in order to accommodate both the object and an amount of sky sufficient to perform reliable background subtraction. In some cases, we tilted the slits to maximize the captured flux. We defined three sets of exposure times/grating combinations, which depend on the surface brightness classes defined above in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2s4\">4</a>:</p><ul class=\"clear-list wd-inline-list\"><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">1.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">R1: 1 hr integration with R150/GG455 grating/filter;</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">2.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">R2: 1 hr integration with B600 grating and 3.7 hr integration with R150/GG455 grating/filter;</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">3.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">R3: 1 hr integration with B600 grating.</div></li></ul><p>\n</p><p>We use the R150 grating in conjunction with the GG455 filter in order to obtain spectra with wavelength coverage ~4500\u201310000 \u00c5. For the sources that we expect to be late-type emission-line galaxies, this would allow us, in most cases, to detect [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>3727 to <em>z</em> ~ 1.7, H<em>\u03b2</em> to <em>z</em> ~ 1.0, and Ly<em>\u03b1</em> in the range <em>z</em> ~ 2.7\u20137.2. We use the B600 grating to obtain spectral coverage of 3250\u20136250 \u00c5, which would allow us to detect sources with <em>z</em> &gt; 2.0 that emit Ly<em>\u03b1</em>.</p><p>A 1 hr observing sequence consisted of a pair of 900 s exposures, followed by a flat field taken with a quartz-halogen lamp and a calibration spectrum taken with a CuAr arc lamp. We then dithered to a different central wavelength to cover the gap between the CCDs and took a CuAr spectrum, followed by the flat-field exposure and then two more 900 s exposures. The 3.7 hr integration used the same sequence repeated 16 times, but with 840 s exposure times. Dividing the integration time into multiple exposures facilitates the removal of cosmic rays. The data were binned 2 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 2, giving effective dispersions of 0.1 and 0.386 nm/pixel for the B600 and R150 gratings, respectively. The low-surface-brightness systems (i.e., rank R3) underwent only 1 hr of integration with the B600 grating. The goal of this work is to confirm and further analyze a set of strong-lensing systems: to conserve telescope time and maximize the number of lensing system confirmations, we elected to not pursue longer integrations for a given candidate system, even if a clear spectroscopic signal did not appear. In addition, the photo-<em>z</em> calibration targets require observations with consistent depth, and thus integration time, across the observation fields.</p><p>We used the Gemini IRAF package v2.16<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2fn14\">60</a></sup>\n to reduce all exposures. In each system, for each wavelength dither, we first process the flat field using the <tt>gsflat</tt> task (this includes subtraction of the bias). Each science exposure in a single dither is then reduced with <tt>gsreduce</tt> (using the previously processed flat fields), and then the two exposures are combined with <tt>gemcombine</tt>. Wavelength calibration and transformation are performed on each dither (using the <tt>gswavelength</tt> and <tt>gstransform</tt> tasks) before the pairs of dithers are coadded on a common wavelength scale to eliminate CCD chip gaps. We perform sky subtraction and one-dimensional (1D) spectral extraction using <tt>gsextract</tt>, which employs the <tt>apall</tt> task. Feature identification and redshift estimation are performed using the <tt>emsao</tt> task within the <tt>rvsao</tt> IRAF package (Kurtz &amp; Mink <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib45\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib45\">1998</a>). We modified some of the Gemini IRAF tasks to provide more flexibility in the data reduction. In particular, we modified <tt>gswavelength</tt> and <tt>gsextract</tt> to allow one to perform 1D and two-dimensional (2D) fits on the calibration data and sky subtraction on the science data, respectively, for individual extensions.</p><p>Of the 21 observed candidate systems, 17 were observed at Gemini: 12 systems were observed in Priority Visiting observer mode from 2014 October 19 to 24, and five systems were observed in queue mode. For nine systems, we obtained all the planned exposures, and for eight systems, we obtained a subset of the planned exposures. The only planned 1 hr integrations acquired with the R150 grating (rank R1) were executed during the Priority Visiting Observer mode. The eight systems for which we did not obtain all planned exposures are missing the planned 3.7 hr R150 observations: in queue mode, these observations had lower Gemini observing priority. All planned 1 hr B600 observations were completed.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjaa23f2s4-2\" name=\"apjaa23f2s4-2\">4.2.\u00a0Magellan/IMACS</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We also obtained spectra at Magellan with IMACS. The mask was again centered on the candidate lensing galaxy of each system. As with GMOS, we used 1''-width slits of varying length. We used the f/2 camera and the 200-<em>\u2113</em>/mm grism, because it has the best response in the redder wavelengths, and we used the WB5650-9200 filter to set the wavelength range to 5650-9200 \u00c5. We took three 1200 s exposures for each mask to facilitate cosmic-ray removal. Two of the systems observed also had a 1 hr integration using the B600 grating using Gemini's GMOS. A ranking system was not used to select which systems to prioritize for observation.</p><p>To process the data, we used the COSMOS data reduction package.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2fn15\">61</a></sup>\n This package performs wavelength calibration, followed by subtraction of bias, and division by flats, using the programs <tt>Sflats</tt> and <tt>biasflat</tt>. The sky is then subtracted using the program <tt>subsky</tt>. Finally, extraction of individual 1D or 2D spectral exposures is performed using <tt>extract</tt>, or <tt>extract-2dspec</tt>. Multiple sets of extracted spectra are then combined using <tt>sumspec</tt>. Feature identification and redshift estimation are performed using the <tt>emsao</tt> IRAF task.</p><p>Of the 21 observed candidate systems, 5 were observed on 2014 December 20\u201321 as part of a larger program to obtain spectroscopic redshifts of (1) supernova hosts and (2) galaxies for photometric redshift calibration of DES data. Note that one system, DES J0329\u20132820, was observed at both Magellan and Gemini.</p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaa23f2s5\" name=\"apjaa23f2s5\">5.\u00a0CONFIRMED LENS SAMPLE</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Of the 24 systems for which we sought follow-up, there was sufficient time to observe 21 systems. Of those, we confirmed a total of six strong-lensing systems. There are 15 systems that were observed but were not confirmed as lenses: nine have no discernible continuum emission (nor spectral features), four have continuum emission but no discernible features, and two were ruled out as lenses.</p><p>A number of the systems that we failed to confirm exhibit clear morphological and photometric lensing features. However, they would require significantly longer integration times or are located in the redshift desert\u2014outside the range of the optical observations in our observing program. This highlights the challenge of obtaining spectra for the very faint objects found in deep optical surveys: a great deal of integration time, in tandem with IR spectrographs, may be required to confirm the large lens samples predicted in current and future large surveys. The candidates that were ruled out as lensing systems indeed exhibit suggestive morphological features, but the candidate lensed sources were determined to be foreground galaxies through spectroscopic analysis.</p><p>A multi-panel plot of the six confirmed systems is shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa23f2f1\">1</a>, and Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2t1\">1</a> lists the positions and photometry of the candidate lens and source(s) of each lensing system observed. The sample comprises one group-scale lens and five cluster-scale lenses. The group-scale lens DES J0221\u20130646 is known from the SARCS sample by SL2S (More et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib57\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib57\">2012</a>), but had not been spectroscopically confirmed by that group. It was found during the nontargeted phase of our visual scan and later identified as a low-richness (&lt;5) group in the redMAPPer catalog. Four lenses (DES J0250\u20130008, DES J0329\u20132820, DES J0446\u20135126, and DES J2336\u20135352) were also identified in the redMAPPer cluster-finder sample. DES J0330\u20135228 (SPT-CL J0330\u20135228/ACT-CL J0330\u20135227; Bleem et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib11\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib11\">2015</a>) is a known candidate lensing systems from the SPT and Atacama Cosmology Telescope (ACT; Kosowsky <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib41\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib41\">2006</a>; Fowler et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib31\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib31\">2007</a>) SZ surveys. DES J2336\u20135352 (SCSO J233607\u2013535235; Menanteau et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib53\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib53\">2010a</a>) is already known from the Southern Cosmology Survey (SCS; Menanteau et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib52\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib52\">2009</a>). However, there were previously no spectroscopic observations of the lensing features in either of these systems. DES J0221\u20130646 and DES J0250\u20130008 were found in the slightly deeper DES supernova fields during the nontargeted searches.</p><p>In this section, we comment on each system, its spectral features of interest, and the derived redshifts. The reduced 1D spectra, alongside cutouts of the fields centered on the central lensing object showing the slit positions, targets, and Einstein radii, are shown for each system in Figures <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa23f2f2\">2</a>\u2013<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa23f2f7\">7</a>. Detailed algorithms do not yield mass model constraints that are signficantly better than enclosed masses (derived from Einstein radii) for systems that have a limited number of sources with multiple, detailed images.</p><p>Therefore, for each system, we employ a strategy similar to that of SBAS (e.g., Diehl et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib25\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib25\">2009</a>) and estimate the enclosed mass <em>M</em><sub>enc</sub> of the lensing system, assuming a singular isothermal sphere mass profile (Narayan &amp; Bartelmann <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa23f2bib59\" id=\"fnref-apjaa23f2bib59\">1996</a>):</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"apjaa23f2eqn1\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/827/1/51/Full/apjaa23f2eqn1.gif\" alt=\"Equation (1)\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray}&&{M}_{\\mathrm{enc}}=\\displaystyle \\frac{{c}^{2}}{4G}{\\theta }_{{\\rm{E}}}^{2}\\left(\\displaystyle \\frac{{D}_{{\\rm{L}}}{D}_{{\\rm{S}}}}{{D}_{\\mathrm{LS}}}\\right),\\end{eqnarray}\n\t\t\t\t\\tag{\n\t\t\t\t1\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t</script></span></div><p>where <em>c</em> is the speed of light, <em>G</em> is Newton's gravitational constant, <em>\u03b8</em><sub>E</sub> is the Einstein radius, and <em>D</em> is the angular diameter distance. We estimate the Einstein radius (or radii if there is more than one source) by manually fitting a circle that passes through one or more spectroscopically confirmed features. The center is chosen to be the center of curvature of the candidate arc image(s). <em>D</em><sub>L</sub>, <em>D</em><sub>S</sub>, and <em>D</em><sub>LS</sub> are angular diameter distances to the lens, to the source, and between the lens and source, respectively: they depend only on the redshifts of these objects and on the cosmological parameters. The spectral features, photometric redshifts of lenses, spectroscopic redshifts of sources, Einstein radii, and enclosed masses are summarized in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaa23f2t3\">3</a>.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaa23f2t3\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 3.</b>\u00a0\nLensing Features\n</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa23f2t3\" data-toolbar-img=\"/0004-637X/827/1/51/suppdata/apjaa23f2t3_lr.gif\" data-toolbar-type=\"table\" data-toolbar-title=\"Table 3\"><colgroup><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col></colgroup><thead>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">System ID and</th>\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Lens Redshift</th>\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Spec.
